<div id="review_34982727" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/34982727" />
    <a title="Marcy Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/263995-marcy-jo"><img alt="Marcy Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532846720p2/263995.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/34982727?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marcy Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marcy Jo" href="/user/show/263995-marcy-jo">Marcy Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">EVERYONE!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/263995-marcy-jo?shelf=signed-copy">signed-copy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer34982727" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11652977973236673525">It goes without saying that I am a lover of books. Stories, characters, and delicious prose...well...these are things that I throw myself into. My shelves are filled with countless books that i have read and loved, stories that I have enjoyed reading.<br/>I have never enjoyed reading a book as much as I enjoyed this one. Never.<br/><br/>It's a scary thing when you get to the final book in a series or trilogy that you particularly care about. There's a certain amount of apprehension involved,correlating directl</span>
  <span id="freeText11652977973236673525" style="display:none">It goes without saying that I am a lover of books. Stories, characters, and delicious prose...well...these are things that I throw myself into. My shelves are filled with countless books that i have read and loved, stories that I have enjoyed reading.<br />I have never enjoyed reading a book as much as I enjoyed this one. Never.<br /><br />It's a scary thing when you get to the final book in a series or trilogy that you particularly care about. There's a certain amount of apprehension involved,correlating directly to your emotional involvement to the story and characters. Its tricky for the author to wrap things up in a way that is true to the characters, consistent with the themes of the previous books, ties up the major and minor story arcs, and is still enjoyable to read. I've never read the final book in any series that managed to seamlessly do all of those things. City of Glass did.<br /><br />The characters in a story like this should be expected to change, to be affected by the events around them, and to react to them in some way. This was handled fantastically!<br /><br />Clary was very Clary-ish. Particularly early on in the book she was just as rash and independent and headstrong as ever. Watching her character progression over the span of the book (as well as the series), I must say that she usurps Gemma Doyle for the crown of female protagonists in the category that I refer to as "Girls Who Do Things." And she does "Do Things." Regardless of the fact that Jace disabled her truck tried to keep her from Idris, despite the fact that she lacks the training or even the in depth knowledge of their society, Clary refuses to sit on the sidelines. She refuses to be relegated to the role of bystander or victim. She was very true to the character that we got to know in City of Bones and City of Ashes.<br /><br />Jace, well, what can I say. Jace's journey here is epic. As he has in every book before, he broke my heart. Watching him struggle with himself, with his past, with things he cannot control...it is beautiful.<br /><br />The 'minor' characters (though I am loathe to call them that, seeing how real and well developed they are) really shine here, too. I can't really elaborate without giving anything away, but WOW. They all grow to meet the challenges before them, and we see a different side of *everyone* in Idris, though they stay true to the characters we knew. To say that I am ecstatic about the character development here is a gross understatement.<br /><br />All of the story arcs--both for the individual characters as well as the main conflicts--are tied up nicely. The foundations for everything that happens have been building since COB. The resolutions are not gratuitous or indulgent. They feel as if--rather than the writer giving the series the ending she wanted it to have, regardless of whether or not it fit the themes of the other books--the author allowed these characters to tell their stories through her. It was the way endings should be...but so rarely ever are. Nothing in this book (or the epilogue) will taint your love for the series...it will grow it.<br /><br />Ashley said that reading City of Glass was like riding a roller coaster in the dark, and she was not wrong. I laughed, I cried, I squealed, I shouted at the characters, I yelled "Yes!" and "No!" Oftentimes I did all of those things within the span of a single chapter. It's an emotional whirlwind reading experience. I was physically unable to put the book down from the moment I picked it up. And the ending? Well, the ending left me breathless.<br /><br />I don't say this lightly: there are probably two dozen books that I easily list as "one of my favorite books of all time."<br /><br />City of Glass is not on that list.<br /><br />City of Glass *IS* my favorite book of all time.<br /><br />For sheer emotional connect, suspense, excitement, character WIN, romance, frighteningly believable villainy goodness, and moments that made me flail around like a toddler in the candy closet, it is unparalleled. Amazing. Wonderful. Fantastic. Words fail me.<br /><br />So for those of you eagerly counting down the days between now and March 24, take heart. City of Glass is well worth the wait. I had really high expectations for it, really high hopes, and it wasn't as good as I thought it would be. It was better.<br /><br />First Read ARC on January 15, 2009<br />Reread 2010, 2011, 2012, 2013</span>
  <a data-text-id="11652977973236673525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1580107684" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1580107684" />
    <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani"><img alt="Ahmad Sharabiani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194930432p2/614778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1580107684?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ahmad Sharabiani" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani">Ahmad Sharabiani</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=21th-century">21th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1580107684" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14300394712349685331">City of Glass (The Mortal Instruments #3), Cassandra Clare<br/><br/><b>City of Glass</b> is the third book in the urban fantasy series <b>The Mortal Instruments</b> by <b>Cassandra Clare</b>. In 2009, Walker Books published the third book of the series worldwide. <br/><br/>Clary is at Luke's house with Simon packing for her trip to Idris, in which both of them have conversations based on Clary's goal to save her mother and the struggle she will face when she reaches Idris. <br/><br/>Jace persuades Simon to lie and say that Clary decided not to g</span>
  <span id="freeText14300394712349685331" style="display:none">City of Glass (The Mortal Instruments #3), Cassandra Clare<br /><br /><b>City of Glass</b> is the third book in the urban fantasy series <b>The Mortal Instruments</b> by <b>Cassandra Clare</b>. In 2009, Walker Books published the third book of the series worldwide. <br /><br />Clary is at Luke's house with Simon packing for her trip to Idris, in which both of them have conversations based on Clary's goal to save her mother and the struggle she will face when she reaches Idris. <br /><br />Jace persuades Simon to lie and say that Clary decided not to go to Idris, in order to protect her from the Clave, who he feels will try to turn her into a weapon. When Clary visits the Institute, Magnus tells her that the Lightwoods had to travel through the portal, due to an attack by Forsaken. <br /><br />During the battle, Simon is injured and Jace takes him to Idris to save his life. With her power to create runes, Clary is able to create a portal and she travels with Luke through the portal. As Simon wakes up to realize that he was pulled through the portal and now is in Alicante, he realizes the truth behind Jace's motivation to not make Clary come to Idris. <br /><br />Later at the Lightwood house, he meets Sebastian Verlac and Aline Penhallow. Over time, Alec comes back from the Clave meeting to tell Simon that he will be sent back to New York by Aldertree, the new Inquisitor. When Simon arrives to leave for home, it is revealed as a trap to bring people back to the Clave's trust and he is imprisoned and is questioned on his new ability to walk in daylight as a vampire. After the questioning, he befriends a fellow mate named Samuel Blackburn. ...<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز چهاردهم ماه دسامبر سال 2018 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: شهر شیشه ای؛ نویسنده: کاساندرا کلر؛ مترجم: نرگس شفاف؛ تهران، اردیبهشت، 1396؛ در 348ص؛ فروست: مجموعه ابزار دوزخی، کتاب سوم؛ شابک 9789641713067؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان امریکایی - سده 21م<br /><br />عنوان: شهر شیشه ای؛ نویسنده: کاساندرا کلر؛ مترجم سعیده کاظمیان؛ تصویرگر سعید فرهنگیان؛ تهران، ویدا، 1398؛ در دو جلد؛ شابک دوره ی دوجلدی 9786002912114؛ <br /><br />کتاب سوم با عنوان:«شهر شیشه ای» از سری داستانهای «ابزارهای فانی (ابزارهای دوزخی)» درباره ی ماجراجویی «کلاری» به همراه «سایمون» در شهر «شکارچیان سایه»، و جستجوی «کلاری»، برای نجات مادر خویش است.«کلاری» برای نجات مادرش، باید به «شهر شیشه ای»، خانه ی اجدادی «شکارچیان سایه» برود.هرگونه ورود غیرمجاز به شهر، خلاف قانون، و سرپیچی از قانون مرگ را بنبال دارد.بدتر از همه «جیس»، اصلا دلش نمیخواهد «کلاری» به آنجا برود، و «سایمون» نیز، توسط «شکارچیان سایه»، زندانی شده است.همانگونه که «کلاری»، درباره ی بگذشته ی خانواده ی خود، بیشتر اطلاعات کسب میکند، به یک حقیقت باورنکرنی نیز دست میباید.«کلاری» متوجه میشود، که یک برادر شیطانی، به نام «سباستین» دارد.اکنون که «ولنتاین» و «سباستین»، میخواهند «شکارچیان سایه» را برای همیشه نابود کنند، تنها یکراه برای رودررویی با آنان وجود دارد، این راه اتحاد بین «زیر زمینیها» و «شکارچیان سایه» است.در این میان، «جیس» نیز به تازگی توانییهای تازه ای یافته است، اما باید دید تا چه اندازه حاضر است، به خاطر «کلاری» خطر کند، و به یاری شهر بشتابد...؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2042319381539094777"><b>My "Epic Book Recipe" Checklist for <i>City of Glass</i>:</b><br/><br/>1. A heroine with just the right amount of emotion whom i like? ☑️<br/><br/>2. An absolutely amazing and swoon-worthy love interest who loves her unconditionally and is my son? ☑️<br/><br/>3. An original setting with a unique and thrilling plot? ☑️<br/><br/>4. A couple of earth-shattering shocks every now and then to keep me on my toes? ☑️<br/><br/>5. Extraordinary side characters with interesting backgrounds? ☑️<br/><br/>6. Desperate circumstances that force me to bite my nails in anxiety? ☑️<br/><br/>7.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4835050567164103724"><b>
  <blockquote>“There is no pretending," Jace said with absolute clarity. "I love you, and I will love you until I die, and if there is life after that, I'll love you then.”</blockquote>
</b> <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466699741i/19509944._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>City of Glass should be the end of this series. I can't believe how I enjoyed this book beyond my expectation. Clary and Jace finally end up and figure their problems out while Alec and Magnus are much more than just flirtatious, they made my heart flutter all the time. Valentine is likewise out of the shadow and does many things to po</span>
  <span id="freeText4835050567164103724" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>“There is no pretending," Jace said with absolute clarity. "I love you, and I will love you until I die, and if there is life after that, I'll love you then.”</blockquote>
</b> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466699741i/19509944._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>City of Glass should be the end of this series. I can't believe how I enjoyed this book beyond my expectation. Clary and Jace finally end up and figure their problems out while Alec and Magnus are much more than just flirtatious, they made my heart flutter all the time. Valentine is likewise out of the shadow and does many things to possess the Shadowhunter world. So this book suprised me to no end with its attractiveness of the characters and great potential of the story. Every turn is worth those minutes I spent.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1466699815ra/19509953.gif" width="400" height="240" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1466699815ra/19509954.gif" width="400" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“And I'm suppose to sit by while you date boys and fall in love with someone else, get married...?" His voice tightened. "And meanwhile, I'll die a little bit more every day, watching.” </blockquote>
</b> <br><br>Can't deny that CoG cracked my heart because of the dialogues. And the ending was beating my brain endlessly when something happened to those characters I loved. Plus I liked the direction of this book; I knew where I had to focus and where I had to let it slip since verything was clear from the first.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1466699917ra/19509959.gif" width="400" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“People aren't born good or bad. Maybe they're born with tendencies either way, but its the way you live your life that matters.”</blockquote>
</b> <br><br>I must say I am clearly satisfied with this book. From the first sentences until the last, it kept my interest all the way.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427472959ra/14274027.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tina ➹ the girl who lives in Fandoms " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tina ➹ the girl who lives in Fandoms " href="/user/show/73227612-tina-the-girl-who-lives-in-fandoms">Tina ➹ the girl who lives in Fandoms </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781481455985" href="/book/show/24885531-city-of-glass">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

<span id="freeTextContainer5925190611043916773"><b>4.5 Golden stars!</b><br/><br/>93%<br/><br/>Finally!!!<br/>We are in the City of Glass!<br/>I was waiting to go there after book one & when I checked all the titles after that, I knew we were getting there soon! & I was unreasonably happy!<br/>here we are!<br/><br/>to be honest, it started boring (Unlike the first 2) as Clary was just wandering around without any special purpose; in half of the book nothing very exciting (action-packed) happened, they were talking, but it has its Fun parts.<br/>but it's getting more and more exciting toward the End</span>
  <span id="freeText5925190611043916773" style="display:none"><b>4.5 Golden stars!</b><br /><br />93%<br /><br />Finally!!!<br />We are in the City of Glass!<br />I was waiting to go there after book one &amp; when I checked all the titles after that, I knew we were getting there soon! &amp; I was unreasonably happy!<br />here we are!<br /><br />to be honest, it started boring (Unlike the first 2) as Clary was just wandering around without any special purpose; in half of the book nothing very exciting (action-packed) happened, they were talking, but it has its Fun parts.<br />but it's getting more and more exciting toward the End. more &amp; more questions, more excitements &amp; more revelations. the battles were petrifying, hair-raising, heart-racing!<br />it's one of my favorite ones in this series, it improved after 50% perfectly! the thrills &amp; the suspension! the reason I give it 5 stars.<br />the BATTLE, the END were my favourite ending so far!<br /><br />&amp; again, All of the characters are awesome; &amp; I love this series for that, I can relate to many characters &amp; I love many of them, even the evil ones are interesting.<br />Alec, Magnus, Simon, Izzy, Raphael, Jace, Luke, Sebastian, Clary, etc, etc!<br /><br />-<br />Plot: ★★★★/5<br />World building; ★★★★★/5<br />Characters: ★★★★★/5<br />Written Style: ★★★★★/5 (more fun)<br />Idea: ★★★★★/5<br />general factors on <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2169284017" rel="nofollow noopener">City of bones</a> review :)</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2242957982" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2242957982" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2242957982?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781481455985" href="/book/show/24885531-city-of-glass">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=otp">otp</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2242957982" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15881743879790682884"><blockquote>#1 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/698699065' rel='nofollow noopener'>City of Bones</a> ★★★★☆<br/>#2 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2242957971' rel='nofollow noopener'>City of Ashes</a> ★★★☆☆<br/>#3 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2242957982' rel='nofollow noopener'>City of Glass</a> ★★★★☆<br/>#4 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2242957998' rel='nofollow noopener'>City of Fallen Angels</a> ★★★★★<br/>#5 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2242958023' rel='nofollow noopener'>City of Lost Souls</a> ★★★★★<br/>#6 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2242958052' rel='nofollow noopener'>City of Heavenly Fire</a> </blockquote><br/>A lot of people told me that the series picked up with book three, and I have to say that those people were absolutely right—this was an easy 4.5-star read and I <i>almost</i> rounded up to 5, even. The pacing was better than the first two books, the character development was delightful, and all of the delicious angst and romance and fighting that Cassie wr</span>
  <span id="freeText15881743879790682884" style="display:none"><blockquote>#1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/698699065" rel="nofollow noopener">City of Bones</a> ★★★★☆<br />#2 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2242957971" rel="nofollow noopener">City of Ashes</a> ★★★☆☆<br />#3 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2242957982" rel="nofollow noopener">City of Glass</a> ★★★★☆<br />#4 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2242957998" rel="nofollow noopener">City of Fallen Angels</a> ★★★★★<br />#5 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2242958023" rel="nofollow noopener">City of Lost Souls</a> ★★★★★<br />#6 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2242958052" rel="nofollow noopener">City of Heavenly Fire</a> </blockquote><br />A lot of people told me that the series picked up with book three, and I have to say that those people were absolutely right—this was an easy 4.5-star read and I <i>almost</i> rounded up to 5, even. The pacing was better than the first two books, the character development was delightful, and all of the delicious angst and romance and fighting that Cassie writes so well was present and accounted for.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> “And now I’m looking at you,” he said, “and you’re asking me if I still want you, as if I could stop loving you. As if I would want to give up the thing that makes me stronger than anything else ever has.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />First, we gotta talk about Jace and Clary. I won’t spoil in this review, but if you’ve read the book, you know about the big twist, and I was so freaking ready for it! I knew it was coming because I’d been spoiled for it back in <i>Bones,</i> but I think knowing it was coming was even better than if I hadn’t, because it was just this fantastic buildup that constantly left me tearing through the next chapter, waiting to get to the big reveal.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> “I know it’s wrong—God, it’s all kinds of wrong—but I just want to lie down with you and wake up with you, just once, just once ever in my life.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />There are <i>so many</i> fantastic moments between the two of them, and even though I know they’re not a tremendously popular one as far as Cassie’s ships go, I’m a sucker for the bad-boy-gone-good, so Jace totally has my heart in this series. He made me <i>cry,</i> like, <i>three times</i>—and okay, yeah, I cry at books a lot anyways, BUT THAT’S BESIDE THE POINT. He’s precious.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> “They didn’t,” Magnus said. “Your wards are down.”<br />“Really?” The Consul’s voice dripped sarcasm. “I hadn’t noticed.”<br />Magnus looked concerned. “That’s terrible. Someone should have told you.” He glanced at Luke. “Tell him the wards are down.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />The real MVP of this series, though, hands down, is Magnus Bane. My god, I know I rambled about him forever in my review for <i>Ashes,</i> too, but I just love this weird little fabulous warlock so much. He’s so damn funny—like, literally makes me laugh out loud in almost every scene he’s in—and he works his witchy little ass off to keep the Shadowhunters safe, even when the Nephilim treat him like garbage half the time. Plus, the development in his romance with a certain Shadowhunter? RIP me, because the cuteness is <b>TOO MUCH.</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> “No,” Simon said. “If you hurt Clary, she’s quite capable of killing you herself. Possibly with a variety of weapons.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />Probably the most unexpected thing for me, though, was how much I grew to tolerate (okay, maybe even <i>like,</i> just a little…) Simon. I couldn’t stand him in either of the first two books, but he grows so much and really comes into his own in this one, and I respected his character development a lot. Something that fascinates me about reading this series is watching just how quickly Cassandra Clare’s writing evolved, between Simon’s shift from lovesick/kicked puppy to actually-not-totally-useless-dude-friend, and Clary/Isabelle’s growing understanding of one another and the way they move away from the trope-y girl-hate that happens a little in <i>Bones.</i><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Magnus looked at Alec as if he’d lost his mind. “Your city is under attack,” he said. “The wards have been broken, and the streets are full of demons. And you want to know why I haven’t called you?”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />Overall, I know this series gets picked at a bit nowadays, because it does fall into some of the standard mid- to late-2000s paranormal fantasy tropes, but honestly, I encourage anyone who hasn’t ever read these books to give them a try. The writing is flawed (though, like I said, quickly improving as I continue reading), and the characters make some pretty idiotic choices every now and again (more like all the time, but it’s part of the charm, I swear), but this series has just been such a fun ride for me. The books are so fun and action-packed, full of angst and drama, and honestly, for the time in which they were published, they’re pretty remarkably well-stocked with diverse characters and representation. They’re not perfect, but they’re certainly worth your time.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> “Good things come to those who wait.”<br />“I always thought that was ‘good things come to those who do the wave’,” said Simon. “No wonder I’ve been so confused all my life.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />(I don’t have anything else to say, I just really liked this quote.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="15881743879790682884" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Ga3mYYrh3IOqjct9iKnLSG2wH+x//enC9GklCeDTQlkD+05bVpA6q9SygTKsvq0gRFogQx3A8n7PJd6qXllHHA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mYUbRGrSp5JZ2ULOnZANwCnJS+3TVYy2otXGuQwNm3yD07N+tqNBuifmCIG5h2uoACN0QrFolwqZmT0asoeeOQ==')})
  }
//]]>

  <span id="freeText715998348368993492" style="display:none">Hello Goodreadsers. Here's my official bio:<br /><br />"Cassandra Clare was born overseas and spent her early years traveling around the world with her family and several trunks of fantasy books. Cassandra worked for several years as an entertainment journalist for the Hollywood Reporter before turning her attention to fiction. She is the author of City of Bones, the first book in the Mortal Instruments trilogy and a New York Times bestseller. Cassandra lives with her fiance and their two cats in Massachusetts."<br /><br />You can find me online at <br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.cassandraclare.com">www.cassandraclare.com</a><br /><br />I have a blog:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://cassandraclare.livejournal.com/">http://cassandraclare.livejournal.com/</a><br /><br />and a Facebook:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.facebook.com/Cassandraclare">http://www.facebook.com/Cassandraclare</a><br /><br />and a Twitter:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.twitter.com/cassieclare">www.twitter.com/cassieclare</a><br /><br />I'll be available here on Goodreads to answer questions for a Goodreads Author Discussion starting September 18 — <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/37113.Q_A_with_Cassandra_Clare">http://www.goodreads.com/group/show/3...</a><br /><br />Go sign up so you don't miss the conversation when it starts!</span>
